## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: materials science (constitutive modeling of mechanical behavior)
**Analysis**: Stress depends on strain and temperature, typical of materials constitutive modeling where stress-strain curves are influenced by strain hardening and thermal softening. The task involves identifying functional forms that describe elastic, plastic, and temperature-dependent behaviors of materials.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Hooke's law (linear elasticity): sigma = c0 * epsilon
- Power-law hardening (Hollomon equation): sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1
- Linear thermal softening of modulus: sigma = c0 * epsilon * (1 - c1 * T)
- Exponential thermal softening: sigma = c0 * epsilon * exp(-c1 * T)
- Voce saturation hardening: sigma = c0 - c1 * exp(-c2 * epsilon)
- Ludwik hardening: sigma = c0 + c1 * epsilon**c2
- Combined power-law hardening with temperature factor: sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 * (1 - c2 * T)
- Power-law with strain offset: sigma = c0 * (epsilon - c1)**c2
- Polynomial with cross-term: sigma = c0 + c1*epsilon + c2*epsilon**2 + c3*T + c4*epsilon*T
- Multiplicative power-law in strain and temperature: sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 * T**c2
- Arrhenius temperature dependence in creep-like form: sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 * exp(c2 / T)
- Sigmoidal yield transition with thermal softening: sigma = c0 / (1 + exp(-c1*(epsilon - c2))) * (1 - c3*T)
- Johnson-Cook type thermal softening (additive form): sigma = (c0 + c1*epsilon**c2) * exp(-c3 * T)
- Temperature-dependent yield with linear hardening: sigma = (c0 - c1*T) + c2*epsilon
- Peak stress with strain (ultimate tensile strength): sigma = c0*epsilon * exp(-c1*epsilon) + c2*epsilon

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Strain hardening: Stress increases monotonically with strain, frequently as a power-law (epsilon**c, 0<c<1) or logarithmic function (ln(1+c*epsilon))
- Thermal softening: Stress decreases with rising temperature, commonly modeled as a multiplicative factor (1 - c*T) or exponential decay (exp(-c*T))
- Yield stress: An additive constant offset in the stress-strain relation represents initial resistance to plastic deformation (sigma = c0 + f(epsilon))
- Saturation hardening: Stress approaches an upper limit with increasing strain, represented by saturating forms like (1 - exp(-c*epsilon)) or Voce equation
- Temperature‑modulated elasticity: The effective elastic modulus decreases with temperature, leading to terms like epsilon * (c0 - c1*T) in the stress expression
- Peak stress and post‑necking softening: A hump in the stress-strain curve (ultimate tensile strength) can be captured by forms such as epsilon * exp(-c*epsilon)
- Elastic-plastic transition: The onset of yielding introduces a smooth transition from linear to nonlinear behavior, modeled by sigmoidal functions or piecewise forms
- Combined hardening and thermal softening: Multiplicative separation f(epsilon) * g(T) is typical, with f increasing and g decreasing, reflecting independent physical mechanisms
- Thermal activation in creep: Slow deformation at high temperature introduces Arrhenius-like factors exp(c/T) combined with a power-law of strain

GT: -c0*(T - c1) + epsilon**c2*c3*(T - c4)
Candidates evaluated: 106

The ground truth (GT) expression is:
`-c0*(T - c1) + epsilon**c2*c3*(T - c4)`
Given that numerically `c1 = c4`, the GT simplifies to:
`(T - c1) * (-c0 + c3 * epsilon**c2)`
Expanding:
`T * (-c0 + c3 * epsilon**c2) + (c0*c1 - c1*c3 * epsilon**c2)`
This is precisely of the form:
`T * (A + B * epsilon^alpha) + C + D * epsilon^alpha`
where `alpha` is a free exponent, and `A, B, C, D` are constants (we are allowed to assign any real values to candidate constants).
The GT uses only the basis functions: `T`, `T*epsilon^alpha`, `1`, `epsilon^alpha`. Any candidate that can be reduced to this form by setting its constants (including zeroing unwanted terms) is a match.

**Analysis of candidates (summary):**
- Candidates lacking a linear `T` term, or having `T` inside nonlinear functions (`sin`, `exp`, `log`, rationals with `T` in denominator that cannot be simplified to linear), can only match if those terms are zeroed and the remainder matches. Most candidates fail because they either miss the `T*epsilon^alpha` term or the `epsilon^alpha` term, or have extra incompatible basis functions that cannot be zeroed without destroying required terms.
- Several candidates, however, naturally contain exactly the required structure or can be reduced to it by setting some constants to zero.

**Explicit matches (among many):**

Since multiple candidates can exactly reproduce the ground truth function by appropriate choice of free constants, the overall verdict is a match.

I need to analyze the Ground Truth (GT) expression and compare it with each candidate.

**GT expression:**
`-c0*(T - c1) + epsilon**c2*c3*(T - c4)`

With c1 = c4 = 352.1579..., so:
`-c0*(T - c1) + c3*epsilon**c2*(T - c1)`
`= (T - c1)*(-c0 + c3*epsilon**c2)`
`= (T - c1)*(c3*epsilon**c2 - c0)`

Expanding:
`= T*c3*epsilon**c2 - c1*c3*epsilon**c2 - c0*T + c0*c1`
`= T*(c3*epsilon**c2 - c0) + (-c1*c3*epsilon**c2 + c0*c1)`

So GT = `T*A*epsilon**c2 + T*B + C*epsilon**c2 + D`

where A = c3 = 1.518..., B = -c0 = -0.5449..., c2 = 0.6261..., C = -c1*c3, D = c0*c1.

The key structural elements are:
- A term `T*epsilon**c2` (product of T and a fractional power of epsilon)
- A term linear in `T`
- A term `epsilon**c2` (same fractional power)
- A constant

This can be written as: `T*a1*epsilon**a2 + T*a3 + a4*epsilon**a2 + a5`

Or equivalently: `T*a1*epsilon**a2 + a4*epsilon**a2 + T*a3 + a5`
